  * On October 13, Israel accused Hamas of violating the ceasefire when it returned the remains of four deceased Israeli hostages; under the agreement, the remains of all hostages in the possession of Palestinian armed groups should be returned on the same day.[187] The plan contains provisions for Hamas to share information with Israel on the deceased hostages that could not be returned within the first 72 hours.[188] Egyptian teams were sent to the Gaza Strip to assist with the location of hostages' bodies.[189] Hamas stated that it faced obstacles in recovering the bodies, as not all burial sites had been identified,[188] bodies remained buried under rubble left by [Israel's bombing of Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_bombing_of_the_Gaza_Strip "Israeli bombing of the Gaza Strip"), as well as lack of access to DNA kits to test the remains.[190][191] On October 25, Trump accused Hamas of refusing to return bodies, alleging: "Some of the bodies are hard to reach, but others they can return now and, for some reason, they are not."[192] As of December 3, 2025, all bodies except one have since been located and returned by Hamas and their junior governing partner, [Palestinian Islamic Jihad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_Islamic_Jihad "Palestinian Islamic Jihad").[193]
  * On October 18, the US State Department stated that it had "credible reports" that Hamas was planning a major imminent attack against Gazan civilians, which it said would constitute a violation of the ceasefire.[194] These comments were understood as a reference to the ongoing crackdown against opposing clans inside Gaza, many of which Israel arms and backs.[195]
  * On October 19, Israel accused Hamas of firing RPGs and sniper fire at Israeli troops stationed in Rafah, killing two IDF soldiers. Hamas denied the accusation, and reports have surfaced that the deaths were caused by an Israeli bulldozer driving over unexploded ordnance, although Israel denied this explanation.[196] Israel proceeded to launch airstrikes. Hamas said that communication with the rest of its units in Rafah had been cut off for months and that, "we are not responsible for any incidents occurring in those areas."[197] Donald Trump indicated that he did not believe Hamas leadership was involved.[198]
  * On October 28, body parts handed over by Hamas to Israel the previous day were identified as belonging to a deceased hostage, whose body was recovered by Israeli forces in November 2023 and additional remains received in March 2024. Prime Minister Netanyahu called it a "clear violation" of the ceasefire.[199] The IDF released a video which it says shows three Hamas militants placing a deceased person underneath rubble, and staging the discovery of the remains of deceased hostage [Ofir Tzarfati](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ofir_Tzarfati "Ofir Tzarfati") to members of the [International Committee of the Red Cross](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross "International Committee of the Red Cross") (ICRC).[199][200] The ICRC issued a statement that it was not aware a cadaver was placed there beforehand and that it was "unacceptable that a fake recovery was staged".[201]
  * On October 28, an IDF official said that its forces were shot at in Rafah and one of its soldiers, who was conducting demolitions at the time, was killed.[202] The IDF stated it returned fire in response. Involvement was denied by Hamas, which reiterated its commitment to the truce.[199][203]
  * On November 19, the IDF said that Hamas had fired on its troops. There were no reported injuries.[204]
  * On December 24, an IDF official said that an explosive was detonated under an IDF vehicle while Israeli soldiers were "dismantling" militant infrastructure, wounding 1 Israeli soldier. Hamas denied responsibility for the explosion and claimed that the explosion was caused by unexploded ordinance.[205]
  * On February 3, 2026, the IDF said that in southern Gaza, packages of humanitarian aid from UNRWA were used for hiding weapons including 110 rockets.[206]
  * On February 4, the IDF said that Hamas militants were filmed using medical vehicles to transport weapons between a hospital and a school.[207]

### By Israel
The [Palestinian Centre for Human Rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_Centre_for_Human_Rights "Palestinian Centre for Human Rights"), a Gaza-based human rights organization, documented at least 129 violations by Israel between October 13 and October 18.[208] In the first 44 days of the ceasefire, Israeli attacks killed 342 Palestinians across 497 ceasefire violations, according to the Gaza Government Media Office.[209] Those killed by Israel are often subsequently accused of approaching the so-called "yellow line" intended to demarcate the boundaries of Israel's withdrawal within Gaza.[210] As well, while the agreement called for 600 trucks of humanitarian aid to enter Gaza per day, Israel allowed an average of 145 trucks to enter per day between October 10 and November 2.[211] As of mid-January 2026, Israeli attacks had killed at least 442 Palestinians and injured 1,240 others.[9]
  * On October 14, Israeli forces killed at least seven Palestinians: six in [Gaza City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_City "Gaza City"), including five by an aerial attack in [Shuja'iyya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shuja%27iyya "Shuja'iyya"), and one by a drone strike in [Khan Yunis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khan_Yunis "Khan Yunis"). The Israeli military said the attacks in Shuja'iyya targeted individuals who advanced beyond the "yellow line" after ignoring warning shots. Hamas spokesperson, Hazem Qassem, condemned the attacks, calling them a violation of the ceasefire agreement.[212]
  * On October 14, Israel closed the [Rafah border crossing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rafah_border_crossing "Rafah border crossing") and stated that the amount of [humanitarian aid allowed into the Gaza Strip](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humanitarian_aid_during_the_Gaza_war "Humanitarian aid during the Gaza war") would be reduced, in response to Hamas's failure to return the remains of all deceased hostages.[213] After four bodies were handed over and further returns were announced for the following day, Israel briefly reversed the restriction.[214] When no further remains were delivered, the crossing was again closed indefinitely. Hamas had earlier stated that recovery efforts were hampered because many burial sites were still unknown amid the extensive destruction in Gaza.[215][216][217] Under the ceasefire terms, Israel was to permit up to 600 humanitarian aid trucks to enter Gaza each day. Since then, the limit had been reduced to 300, with Israeli officials attributing the change to ongoing delays in locating and recovering hostages' remains.[218] Data from the UN2720 Monitoring and Tracking Dashboard, which records the movement of humanitarian convoys entering Gaza, showed that between October 10 and 16, 216 trucks reached their intended destinations within the Gaza Strip.[218]
  * On October 17, Israeli forces opened fire on a bus carrying members of the Abu Shaaban family in the Zeitoun neighbourhood of Gaza City, killing 11 of them, including women and children. The IDF stated that the vehicle entered a restricted area and ignored multiple warning shots.[219][220][221]
  * On October 19, the IDF carried out airstrikes across the Gaza Strip.[222] An Israeli airstrike killed two Palestinians in eastern [Jabalia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jabalia "Jabalia").[223] According to [Channel 12](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Channel_12_\(Israel\) "Channel 12 \(Israel\)"), the attack in Rafah was intended to protect members of the [Popular Forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_Forces "Popular Forces"), an Israeli-backed gang[224] led by [Yasser Abu Shabab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yasser_Abu_Shabab "Yasser Abu Shabab") that is accused of looting humanitarian aid entering the Gaza Strip.[224][225] An Israeli airstrike also killed six Palestinians in the central Gaza city of [Zuwayda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Az-Zawayda "Az-Zawayda"). Those killed in the strike were members of Hamas's [al-Qassam Brigades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qassam_Brigades "Al-Qassam Brigades"), including Yahya al-Mabhouh, the commander of [Hamas's elite unit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nukhba_forces "Nukhba forces") in the Jabalia Battalion.[226] Additionally, two separate strikes killed six more people, including children, near [Nuseirat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuseirat "Nuseirat") in central Gaza, with 13 others injured. Further, a woman and two children were killed in a drone strike that hit a tent accommodating displaced persons near the town of Asda, located north of Khan Yunis. By the end of the day, Israeli airstrikes had killed at least 45 people.[222] The IDF stated that strikes were a response to a violation of the agreement, alleging that two soldiers had been killed in an attack in Rafah.
  * On October 28, Israeli attacks in Gaza killed at least 104 people, at least 66 of whom were children and women.[202][227] The IDF stated that it was targeting Hamas, including 21 militants who allegedly participated in the 7 October attacks. Israeli forces later said that the truce was back on in Gaza.[203] The IDF also stated that the attack was a response to two incidents that occurred on the same day, the return by Hamas of body parts previously repatriated to Israel, and an attack on IDF soldiers in Rafah that left one soldier dead. Hamas denied involvement in the attack on soldiers.[203][199] Hamas said that it postponed the planned handover of the remains of a deceased hostage it had recovered.[199]
  * On October 29, an Israeli attack killed two people in [Beit Lahia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beit_Lahia "Beit Lahia"). According to Israel, the attack targeted a site storing weapons that posed "an immediate threat" to Israeli forces.[228]
  * On November 2, a Palestinian man was killed by an Israeli drone in Shuja'iyya. Israel alleged that he had crossed the "yellow line".[229]
  * On November 10, two Palestinians, including a child, were killed by an Israeli drone strike in east [Khan Yunis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khan_Yunis "Khan Yunis"). The IDF said that the Palestinians killed posed "an immediate threat" to Israeli forces.[230]
  * On November 19, Israel launched several airstrikes in Gaza, targeting [Zaytun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zaytun_Quarter "Zaytun Quarter"), [Shuja'iyya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shuja%27iyya "Shuja'iyya") and Khan Yunis.[204] These attacks killed 33 people, including 17 in Khan Yunis and 16 in Gaza City, with 77 others injured.[231][232]
  * On November 22, the Israeli military launched airstrikes in Gaza, killing at least 24 people: eleven in [Rimal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rimal "Rimal"), three at a house near [Al-Awda Hospital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Awda_Hospital "Al-Awda Hospital"), seven (including a child) at a house in [Nuseirat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuseirat_refugee_camp "Nuseirat refugee camp"), and three at a house in [Deir al-Balah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deir_al-Balah "Deir al-Balah"); another 54 were injured by the attacks. According to Israel, the strikes targeted Hamas militants and killed five senior members.[233]
  * On November 24, four people were killed by Israeli forces, including a man killed by a drone attack in [Bani Suheila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bani_Suheila "Bani Suheila") and a child killed in northern Gaza City after ordnances left by the IDF exploded.[234]
  * On November 29, two Palestinian children were killed while collecting firewood by an Israeli drone strike on the town of Bani Suhayla, east of Khan Yunis, near Al-Farabi School.[235][236][237] The area targeted in the attack lies beyond the so-called Yellow Line, the demarcation line for the redeployment of Israeli forces.[238]
  * On November 29, Israeli airstrikes were carried out in Rafah and Khan Yunis. Israeli fighter jets carried out strikes east of the city of Rafah.[239]
  * On December 3, an Israeli strike targeted a shelter camp in [Al-Mawasi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Mawasi,_Rafah "Al-Mawasi, Rafah"), killing five Palestinians, including two children and injuring several others. Israel said that it struck a Hamas target in response to an alleged clash between Palestinian militants and IDF forces.[240]
  * On December 5, the Israeli military, using helicopter gunships, launched an assault on the eastern and northeastern regions of Khan Yunis, in violation of the ceasefire.[241]
  * On December 7, a three-year-old girl was killed by the Israeli military while playing in her family's tent in Al-Mawasi. The IDF later issued a statement that it was "not aware of a strike" but would "conduct an additional review".[242]
  * On December 18, Israeli forces fired a mortar shell into a residential area in Gaza City during an operation on the Yellow Line, injuring at least 10 people.[243]
  * On December 19, five Palestinians, including a baby, were killed by Israeli soldiers over the Yellow Line in [Tuffah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tuffah "Tuffah"), Gaza City. Israeli forces said that they identified "a number of suspicious individuals … in command structures west of the Yellow Line". The IDF also stated that is "under review" and "regrets any harm to uninvolved individuals."[244]
  * On December 25, three Palestinians were killed by Israeli forces after, according to the IDF, crossing the Yellow Line and "posing a threat" to them.[245]
  * On January 4, 2026, Gaza health authorities reported three Palestinians including a 15-year-old boy and a fisherman were killed by Israeli forces in Khan Yunis.[246]
  * On January 8, at least 13 people, including five children, were killed by Israeli attacks in various locations in the Gaza.[247] Israeli forces said that earlier that day, a projectile was launched "from the area of Gaza City toward the state of Israel" before it fell within the Gaza Strip.[248]
  * On January 11, three people were killed and nine others were injured in various locations in the Gaza Strip by Israeli forces.[249]
  * On January 12, an Israeli quadcopter drone targeted and killed three Palestinians and a woman was injured by Israeli gunfire in Khan Yunis.[250]
  * On January 15, _[Wafa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wafa "Wafa")_ reported that the six Palestinians, including a 16-year-old child were killed by Israeli forces on two homes in [Deir al-Balah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deir_al-Balah "Deir al-Balah"), with the IDF claimed that one of the victims was Muhammad al-Hawli, a commander of [Al-Qassam Brigades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qassam_Brigades "Al-Qassam Brigades").[251][252] Additionally, Israeli forces killed one person at a roundabout in Rafah, another on a police post in Gaza City and two more from an Israeli air attack on a home in the [Nuseirat refugee camp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuseirat_refugee_camp "Nuseirat refugee camp").[251]
  * On January 21, a father, his 13-year-old son, and a 22-year-old man were killed in an IDF drone strike; three journalists, including a member of the [Agence France-Presse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agence_France-Presse "Agence France-Presse") (AFP) traveling in an Egyptian Aid Committee vehicle, were killed by Israeli fire.[253] The Israeli military stated they targeted "suspects" operating a drone affiliated with Hamas, which they deemed was a threat to troops. In a separate incident that day, a 13-year-old boy was reportedly shot and killed while gathering wood for cooking fuel. In total, 11 people were killed on that day by Israel.[254]
  * On January 25, the Gaza health ministry reported that three Palestinians were killed by Israeli forces, two in Tuffah and one in Khan Yunis. That same day, four people were injured by an Israeli drone in Gaza City.[255]
  * On January 30, five Palestinians were killed and eleven others were injured by Israeli attacks, two by a drone in the [Maghazi refugee camp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maghazi_refugee_camp "Maghazi refugee camp") and three others in Rafah. The IDF stated that the strike in Rafah targeted "terrorists"from an underground location.[256]
  * On January 31, Israeli strikes targeted various locations in the Gaza Strip, killing at least 32 people, including 14 people at a police station in Gaza City, as well as two women and six children from two different families. The IDF stated that those strikes followed two separate ceasefire violations a day earlier, in which Israeli forces killed three militants who emerged from a tunnel in an Israeli-controlled area of Rafah, and four who approached troops near the dividing line.[257][258][259]
  * On February 4, at least 24 Palestinians, including two infants, were killed by Israeli strikes. Israel said that the strikes were a response after a militant attack on Israeli soldiers that seriously injured one, and targeted at least two militant commanders, three people who posed danger to its forces, and militant whom it accused of killing a soldier hostage.[260]
  * On February 9, seven people were killed by Israeli forces, including four that were killed after a residential building for displaced people in [Nasser, Gaza City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nasser,_Gaza_City "Nasser, Gaza City") was attacked by Israel.[261]
  * On February 10, two Palestinians were killed by an Israeli drone while cycling in eastern Deir al-Balah near the ceasefire line.[262]
  * On February 15, at least 11 people were killed by Israeli forces in the [Jabalia refugee camp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jabalia_refugee_camp "Jabalia refugee camp") and in Khan Yunis.[263] _Al Jazeera_ reported that a commander of the [Palestinian Islamic Jihad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_Islamic_Jihad "Palestinian Islamic Jihad"), Sami al-Dahdouh, was also killed by Israel in [Tel al-Hawa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_al-Hawa "Tel al-Hawa"), Gaza City.[263] The IDF stated that the attacks struck "terror targets" in response to ceasefire violations by Hamas, saying that militants who had entered the Israeli-controlled area of the strip through a tunnel had been killed.[264]
  * On February 21, Israeli airstrikes targeted the Jabalia refugee camp and [Qizan an-Najjar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qizan_an-Najjar "Qizan an-Najjar"), killing two people. Israeli forces stated on [X](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twitter "Twitter") that the attacks targeted a fighter who crossed that demarcation line in northern Gaza and approached them "in a manner that posed an immediate threat."[265]
  * On February 27, Israeli drones targeted two police posts in the [Bureij refugee camp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bureij "Bureij") and [Al-Mawasi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Mawasi,_Rafah "Al-Mawasi, Rafah"), killing six people.[266]
  * On March 7, a man and his daughter were killed by an Israeli drone in Khan Yunis.[267]
  * On March 15, at least 13 Palestinians, including two children, a pregnant woman and nine police officers, were killed by Israeli airstrikes in various locations in the Gaza Strip.[268]
  * On March 22, three members of the local police and a senior member of an armed group linked to [Fatah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatah "Fatah") were killed by Israeli airstrikes in Nuseirat and [Sheikh Radwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheikh_Radwan "Sheikh Radwan") respectively.[269]

## Opinions
According to an analysis published in _[The Wall Street Journal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal "The Wall Street Journal")_ , Hamas's shift towards agreeing to the peace deal was primarily driven by growing diplomatic pressure both from within and outside the group. This pressure stemmed from Arab and other Muslim countries, especially Turkey, Egypt, and Qatar, who urged Hamas to accept the agreement. Their pressure was influenced by Trump's efforts and by the Israeli attacks in Lebanon, Iran, and Qatar, which heightened fears in the Arab world of Israel's growing power. Additionally, Hamas faced pressure at home, where the people in Gaza were suffering from hunger and destruction and simply wanted the war to end. These factors combined to force Hamas into agreeing to release the hostages and sign the first part of the peace deal, as it saw no other way to end the war.[270]
Historian [Rashid Khalidi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rashid_Khalidi "Rashid Khalidi") stated on October 13, 2025, that Trump's plan was not a genuine peace process, since it consisted of a [ceasefire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ceasefire "Ceasefire"), a [hostage exchange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prisoner_exchange "Prisoner exchange"), and a temporary lift of the [Israeli blockade of Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip_\(2023%E2%80%93present\) "Israeli blockade of the Gaza Strip \(2023–present\)"), but did not contain plans for "completely equal rights for all individuals and both peoples".[271] Belén Fernández wrote in [Al Jazeera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Jazeera_English "Al Jazeera English") that Tony Blair's inclusion in the transitional government "smacks rather hard of [colonialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonialism "Colonialism")" and that Blair's support for the [2003 invasion of Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq "2003 invasion of Iraq") should preclude him from any role on the "Board of Peace".[272] _[The Guardian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian "The Guardian")_ wrote that the plan does not provide Palestinians with "meaningful agency" and "risks freezing subjugation under the language of peace".[273] Human rights attorney [Noura Erakat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noura_Erakat "Noura Erakat") said that the goal of the plan is to "force outcomes onto the Palestinian people".[274] [Diana Buttu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diana_Buttu "Diana Buttu"), a former spokesperson for the PLO, said the plan "normalised genocide".[275]
## Reactions
### Palestine and Israel
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Hostages_Square_09102025_11.jpg/250px-Hostages_Square_09102025_11.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Hostages_Square_09102025_11.jpg)[Hostages Square](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hostages_Square "Hostages Square") in Tel Aviv, October 9, 2025, following the announcement of the impending release of Israeli hostages. Artwork says "[Matan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matan_Angrest "Matan Angrest") [Angrest] is coming home!". [![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Teddi_stadium_-_thank_you_president_Trump.jpg/250px-Teddi_stadium_-_thank_you_president_Trump.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Teddi_stadium_-_thank_you_president_Trump.jpg)[Teddy Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teddy_Stadium "Teddy Stadium") with sign "Thank you president Trump"
Support in the Israeli government was mixed. Finance Minister [Bezalel Smotrich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bezalel_Smotrich "Bezalel Smotrich") denounced the plan as "a historic missed opportunity" which will force Israel to "fight in Gaza again".[1] Leader of the Opposition [Yair Lapid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yair_Lapid "Yair Lapid") endorsed the plan and said, "Israel should announce it is joining the discussions led by the president to finalize the details of the deal."[276]
Israeli opposition politician [Benny Gantz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benny_Gantz "Benny Gantz") lauded "Trump's extraordinary efforts to secure a hostage deal and safeguard Israeli security" and said the plan "must be implemented, our hostages brought home, Israel's operational freedom maintained, Hamas's terror regime in Gaza replaced, and moderate Arab States instated instead as I proposed a year and a half ago".[277]
On October 12, 2025, Israeli Prime Minister [Benjamin Netanyahu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu "Benjamin Netanyahu") warned that the "military campaign is not over" and that Israel's enemies were "trying to recover in order to attack us again".[278][279] Defense Minister [Israel Katz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_Katz "Israel Katz") announced that "Israel's great challenge after the phase of returning the hostages will be the destruction of all of Hamas' terror tunnels in Gaza."[280] Katz said he "instructed the IDF to prepare to carry out the mission".[281]
The [Palestinian Authority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_Authority "Palestinian Authority") called Trump's efforts "sincere and determined" and said that it is committed to holding new parliamentary and presidential elections within a year of the war's end, changing school curriculum, and forming a new security force, while affirming its desire for a "modern, democratic, and non-militarized Palestinian state, committed to pluralism and the peaceful transfer of power".[282]
Taher al-Nounou, a senior Hamas official, said in September they were not consulted about the current proposal and, in any case, they will not accept the demilitarization offer as Israel has demanded.[2][3] Hamas leader in Gaza, [Izz al-Din al-Haddad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Izz_al-Din_al-Haddad "Izz al-Din al-Haddad"), reportedly objected to the proposal as he is thought to believe that the plan aims to finish Hamas. Hamas's political leadership in Qatar have been reported to be open to accepting the proposal with certain amendments.[82] On October 3, 2025, Hamas issued an official response, declaring its readiness to release all hostages, to hand over the administration of the Gaza Strip to independent Palestinian technocrats and to negotiate further details.[5]
[Palestinian Islamic Jihad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_Islamic_Jihad "Palestinian Islamic Jihad") (PIJ) leader [Ziyad al-Nakhalah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ziyad_al-Nakhalah "Ziyad al-Nakhalah") called the plan an attempt by Israel to impose through the U.S. "what it could not achieve through war" and condemned "the American-Israeli declaration" as "a recipe for blowing up the region".[1] Following Hamas's agreement to the plan, the PIJ followed suit and said Hamas's response "represents the stance of the Palestinian resistance forces".[283]
In the [Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_Front_for_the_Liberation_of_Palestine "Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine"), senior member Abu Ali Hassan, said that the plan is "a recipe for managing the war and prolonging it, not for its end". He also called the plan "a desperate attempt to separate Gaza from the Palestinian territorial entity".[284]
### International
[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Family_photo_of_the_2025_Sharm_El-Sheikh_Peace_Summit_%28Daniel_Torok%29.jpg/250px-Family_photo_of_the_2025_Sharm_El-Sheikh_Peace_Summit_%28Daniel_Torok%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Family_photo_of_the_2025_Sharm_El-Sheikh_Peace_Summit_\(Daniel_Torok\).jpg)[Gaza peace summit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2025_Gaza_peace_summit "2025 Gaza peace summit") on October 13, 2025
International leaders widely welcomed the ceasefire, affirmed its importance, and hoped it would lead to lasting peace.[285][286] [Argentine president](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Argentina "President of Argentina") [Javier Milei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Javier_Milei "Javier Milei") stated that Trump should be awarded the [Nobel Peace Prize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize "Nobel Peace Prize").[287] [Canadian prime minister](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada "Prime Minister of Canada") [Mark Carney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Carney "Mark Carney") praised the efforts of Trump, Qatar, Egypt, and Turkey in negotiating the agreement and called on Israel and Hamas to carry out their commitment to free all hostages.[288] The collective [presidency of Bosnia and Herzegovina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidency_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina "Presidency of Bosnia and Herzegovina") unanimously decided to nominate Trump for the Nobel Peace Prize for his "commitment to establishing lasting peace in Gaza" and the Middle East, marking this the first official nomination for the 2026 edition of the award.[289]
Immediately following the release of the hostages, U.S. President Trump visited Israel and addressed Israel's Parliament, the [Knesset](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knesset "Knesset"), celebrating the release of hostages and calling for a commitment to end fighting and rebuild Gaza.[290] He described the ceasefire as marking "not only the end of war, but the end of an age of terror and death and the beginning of the age of faith and hope and of God", and stated that Israel had "won all that it can by force of arms… Now it is time to translate these victories… into the ultimate prize of peace and prosperity for the entire Middle East."[291] He urged Palestinians to "turn forever from the path of terror and violence" and extended an appeal to Iran for "friendship and cooperation". Trump also highlighted the role of Arab and Muslim countries in pressuring Hamas to release hostages, calling it "an incredible triumph for Israel to have all these nations working together as partners in peace".[291]
On October 6, 2025, [High Representative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy "High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy") [Kaja Kallas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaja_Kallas "Kaja Kallas") announced that the [European Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union "European Union") seeks a role in the proposed transitional authority for Gaza, stating, "we feel that Europe has a great role and we should be also on board with this."[292] The European Union has two overseas operations in the Palestinian territories, the [European Union Border Assistance Mission to Rafah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union_Border_Assistance_Mission_to_Rafah "European Union Border Assistance Mission to Rafah") and the [European Union Mission for the Support of Palestinian Police and Rule of Law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union_Mission_for_the_Support_of_Palestinian_Police_and_Rule_of_Law "European Union Mission for the Support of Palestinian Police and Rule of Law"). 
The [United Nations special rapporteur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_special_rapporteur "United Nations special rapporteur") for human rights "expressed hope for a permanent ceasefire", but said that multiple portions of the plan contradicted international law and the [ICJ advisory opinion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ICJ_case_on_Israel%27s_occupation_of_the_Palestinian_territories "ICJ case on Israel's occupation of the Palestinian territories") on Israel's occupation of Palestine.[293]
On October 23, 2025, the [Knesset](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knesset "Knesset") passed a [preliminary reading](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reading_\(legislature\) "Reading \(legislature\)") of bill that would extend [Israeli sovereignty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proposed_Israeli_annexation_of_the_West_Bank "Proposed Israeli annexation of the West Bank") to all [Israeli settlements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_settlement "Israeli settlement") in the West Bank.[294] The bill was condemned by Secretary of State [Marco Rubio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marco_Rubio "Marco Rubio") as "counterproductive" to Trump's Gaza peace plan. Trump added that "Israel would lose all of its support from the United States if that happened."[295]
In October 2025, [Steven Fagin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steven_Fagin "Steven Fagin"), who previously served as the [U.S. ambassador to Yemen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_ambassadors_of_the_United_States_to_Yemen "List of ambassadors of the United States to Yemen"), was designated as the civilian leader of the [Civil-Military Coordination Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil-Military_Coordination_Center "Civil-Military Coordination Center") to facilitate the implementation of the peace plan. Secretary of State Marco Rubio visited the center located in [Kiryat Gat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kiryat_Gat "Kiryat Gat"), which is 56 kilometers (34.7 miles) south of [Tel Aviv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv "Tel Aviv"), and remarked that the center demonstrated a "healthy optimism" regarding advancements in the implementation of the ceasefire.[296]
Tens of thousands of individuals have taken to the streets in various cities throughout Europe to commemorate the UN International Day of Solidarity with the Palestinian People in November 2025, urging for more robust global measures to address the persistent and lethal breaches of the US-mediated ceasefire.[297]
On November 27, 2025, [Amnesty International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amnesty_International "Amnesty International") released a report stating that despite the ceasefire, Israel continues to commit a genocide in the Gaza Strip by continuing to purposefully inflict conditions of life meant to bring about their bodily annihilation.[298][299]

[Gaza war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_war "Gaza war")  
---  
Part of the [Gaza–Israel conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza%E2%80%93Israel_conflict "Gaza–Israel conflict"), the [Israeli–Palestinian conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict "Israeli–Palestinian conflict"), and the [Middle Eastern crisis (2023–present)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Eastern_crisis_\(2023%E2%80%93present\) "Middle Eastern crisis \(2023–present\)")

Diplomacy and [peace proposals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Middle_East_peace_proposals "List of Middle East peace proposals") in the [Arab–Israeli conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_normalization "Arab–Israeli normalization")

Background| 
  * 1914 [Damascus Protocol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Damascus_Protocol "Damascus Protocol")
  * 1915 [McMahon–Hussein correspondence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McMahon%E2%80%93Hussein_correspondence "McMahon–Hussein correspondence")
  * 1916 [Sykes–Picot Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sykes%E2%80%93Picot_Agreement "Sykes–Picot Agreement")
  * 1917 [Balfour Declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balfour_Declaration "Balfour Declaration")
  * 1918 [Declaration to the Seven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declaration_to_the_Seven "Declaration to the Seven") / [Anglo-French Declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-French_Declaration "Anglo-French Declaration")
  * 1919 [Faisal–Weizmann agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faisal%E2%80%93Weizmann_agreement "Faisal–Weizmann agreement")
  * 1920 [San Remo conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Remo_conference "San Remo conference")
  * 1922 [Churchill White Paper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Churchill_White_Paper "Churchill White Paper")
  * 1937 [Peel Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peel_Commission "Peel Commission")
  * 1939 [White Paper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Paper_of_1939 "White Paper of 1939")
  * 1939 [London Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London_Conference_of_1939 "London Conference of 1939")
  * 1946 [Morrison–Grady Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morrison%E2%80%93Grady_Plan "Morrison–Grady Plan")
  * 1947 [Bevin Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bevin_Plan "Bevin Plan")
  * 1946–47 [London Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London_Conference_of_1946%E2%80%931947 "London Conference of 1946–1947")
  * 1947 [UN Partition Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Partition_Plan_for_Palestine "United Nations Partition Plan for Palestine")
  * 1948 [American trusteeship proposal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_trusteeship_proposal_for_Palestine "American trusteeship proposal for Palestine")

  
1948–1988| 
  * 1948 [UN General Assembly (UNGA) Resolution 194](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_194 "United Nations General Assembly Resolution 194")
  * 1949 [Armistice agreements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements "1949 Armistice Agreements") / [Lausanne Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lausanne_Conference_of_1949 "Lausanne Conference of 1949")
  * 1950 [Tripartite Declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tripartite_Declaration_of_1950 "Tripartite Declaration of 1950")
  * 1967 [Khartoum Resolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khartoum_Resolution "Khartoum Resolution") / [UN Security Council (UNSC) Resolution 242](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_242 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 242")
  * 1971 [UNSC Resolution 298](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_298 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 298")
  * 1973 [UNSC Resolution 338](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_338 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 338") / [UNSC Resolution 339](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_339 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 339")
  * 1974 [Israel–Syria disengagement agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agreement_on_Disengagement_between_Israel_and_Syria "Agreement on Disengagement between Israel and Syria") / [UNSC Resolution 350](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_350 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 350")
  * 1978 [UNSC Resolution 425](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_425 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 425") / [Camp David Accords](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_David_Accords "Camp David Accords")
  * 1979 [UNSC Resolution 446](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_446 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 446") / [Egypt–Israel peace treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt%E2%80%93Israel_peace_treaty "Egypt–Israel peace treaty") [Palestinian autonomy talks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_autonomy_talks "Palestinian autonomy talks") / [UNSC Resolution 452](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_452 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 452")
  * 1980 [UNSC Resolution 478](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_478 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 478") / [Venice Declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venice_Declaration "Venice Declaration")
  * 1981 [UNSC Resolution 497](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_497 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 497")
  * 1981–1982 [Fahd Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fahd_Plan "Fahd Plan")
  * 1982 [Reagan peace plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reagan_peace_plan "Reagan peace plan")
  * 1983 [Israel–Lebanon agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/May_17_Agreement "May 17 Agreement")
  * 1987 [Peres–Hussein London Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peres%E2%80%93Hussein_London_Agreement "Peres–Hussein London Agreement") / [Amirav-Husseini peace meetings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amirav-Husseini_peace_meetings "Amirav-Husseini peace meetings")
  * 1988 [1988 Shultz Initiative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988_Shultz_Initiative "1988 Shultz Initiative") / [1988 Yasser Arafat speech to the United Nations General Assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988_Yasser_Arafat_speech_to_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly "1988 Yasser Arafat speech to the United Nations General Assembly")
  * 1990 [Saddam Hussein initiative of 12 August 1990](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saddam_Hussein_initiative_of_12_August_1990 "Saddam Hussein initiative of 12 August 1990")

  
1991–2016| 
  * 1991 [Madrid Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madrid_Conference_of_1991 "Madrid Conference of 1991")
  * 1993 [Oslo Accords](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oslo_Accords "Oslo Accords")

  * 1994 [Gaza–Jericho Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza%E2%80%93Jericho_Agreement "Gaza–Jericho Agreement") / [Israel–Jordan peace treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Jordan_peace_treaty "Israel–Jordan peace treaty")
  * 1995 [Beilin–Abu Mazen agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beilin%E2%80%93Abu_Mazen_agreement "Beilin–Abu Mazen agreement")

  * 2002 [Beirut Summit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_Arab_League_summit "2002 Arab League summit") and [peace initiative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Peace_Initiative "Arab Peace Initiative") / [Road map](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Road_map_for_peace "Road map for peace") / [Elon Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elon_Peace_Plan "Elon Peace Plan")
  * 2003 [Geneva Initiative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geneva_Initiative "Geneva Initiative")
  * 2004 [UNSC Resolution 1559](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1559 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 1559") / [UNSC Resolution 1566](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1566 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 1566")
  * 2005 [UNSC Resolution 1583](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1583 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 1583") / [Sharm El Sheikh Summit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005_Sharm_El_Sheikh_Summit "2005 Sharm El Sheikh Summit") / [Israeli disengagement from the Gaza Strip](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_disengagement_from_the_Gaza_Strip "Israeli disengagement from the Gaza Strip") / [Agreement on Movement and Access](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip#2005_Agreement_on_Movement_and_Access "Blockade of the Gaza Strip") / [Valley of Peace initiative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valley_of_Peace_initiative "Valley of Peace initiative")
  * 2006 [UNSC Resolution 1850](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1850 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 1850") / [Quartet Principles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quartet_Principles "Quartet Principles")
  * 2006 [UNSC Resolution 1701](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1701 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 1701")
  * 2007 [Annapolis Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annapolis_Conference "Annapolis Conference")
  * 2010 [Israeli–Palestinian peace talks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010%E2%80%932011_Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_peace_talks "2010–2011 Israeli–Palestinian peace talks")
  * 2011 [Israeli Peace Initiative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Peace_Initiative "Israeli Peace Initiative")

| [Background](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intercommunal_conflict_in_Mandatory_Palestine "Intercommunal conflict in Mandatory Palestine")| 
| 1920–1948| 
  * 1920 
    * [Nebi Musa riots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1920_Nebi_Musa_riots "1920 Nebi Musa riots")
    * [Battle of Tel Hai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Tel_Hai "Battle of Tel Hai")
  * 1921 [Jaffa riots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaffa_riots_\(May_1921\) "Jaffa riots \(May 1921\)")
  * 1929 [Palestine riots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1929_Palestine_riots "1929 Palestine riots")
    * [Hebron massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1929_Hebron_massacre "1929 Hebron massacre")
  * 1936–1939 [Arab revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936%E2%80%931939_Arab_revolt_in_Palestine "1936–1939 Arab revolt in Palestine")
  * 1944–1947 [Jewish insurgency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_insurgency_in_Mandatory_Palestine "Jewish insurgency in Mandatory Palestine")
  * 1947–1948 [Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1947%E2%80%931948_civil_war_in_Mandatory_Palestine "1947–1948 civil war in Mandatory Palestine") / [Nakba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nakba "Nakba")

| 1948–1970|

    * 1951–1967 [Attacks against Israeli civilians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_attacks_against_Israeli_civilians_before_1967 "List of attacks against Israeli civilians before 1967")
    * 1950s–1960s [Reprisal operations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reprisal_operations "Reprisal operations")
  * 1949–1956 [Palestinian expulsions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1949%E2%80%931956_Palestinian_expulsions "1949–1956 Palestinian expulsions")
  * 1953 [Qibya massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qibya_massacre "Qibya massacre")
  * 1956 [Suez Crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis "Suez Crisis") / [Kafr Qasim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kafr_Qasim_massacre "Kafr Qasim massacre") / [Khan Yunis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khan_Yunis_massacre "Khan Yunis massacre") / [Rafah massacres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1956_Rafah_massacre "1956 Rafah massacre")
